Special Inspection Report 
FY20 MILCON Project P-463 
SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility 
Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam (JBPHH) 
Pearl City Peninsula, Oahu, Hawaii 
Dear Mr. Monahan: 
In accordance with the Subcontract for Professional Services between Hensel 
Phelps Construction Co. and Geolabs, Inc. entered into on April 23, 2020 (Subcontract 
No. 6020071-01 00700), we observed the driven pile foundation installation operations 
for the FY20 MILCON P-463 SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility project 
located at Pearl City Peninsula on the Island of Oahu from November 2, 2020 through 
January 7, 2021.  
Geolabs provided “Special Inspection” services by observing the indicator pile 
program, static load tests, and production pile installation in general accordance with 
Section 1705.7 of the 2018 International Building Code. The attached Driven Pile 
Foundation Installation Report dated July 30, 2021 summarizes our field observations 
and related information. 
To the best of our knowledge, it is our professional opinion that the driven pile 
foundation installation work for the SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility project 
at Pearl City Peninsula observed by Geolabs has been constructed in general 
conformance with the approved plans and specifications, the geotechnical engineering 
report prepared for the project, and our subsequent recommendations. The constructed 
driven pile foundation observed by Geolabs should be capable of providing the 
allowable design load capacity. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co.

Reference: Report by Geolabs, Inc. dated October 29,2020

FY20 MILCON Project P-463 
SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility 
Pearl City Peninsula, JBPHH, Oahu, Hawaii 
Dear Mr. Monahan: 
In accordance with our Subcontract for Professional Services entered into on 
April 23, 2020 with Hensel Phelps Construction Co, Geolabs observed the indicator pile 
program, static load tests, and production pile installation of the driven pile foundations 
for the FY20 MILCON P-463 SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility project. This 
letter report summarizes our geotechnical observations during the driven pile foundation 
installation for the FY20 MILCON P-463 SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility 
project within Joint Base Pearl Harbor-Hickam (JBPHH) at Pearl City Peninsula, Oahu, 
Hawaii. 
Geolabs provided geotechnical engineering services and served as the 
Geotechnical Designer-of-Record (DOR) for the FY20 MILCON P-463 SOF Undersea 
Operational Training Facility project. The purpose of our geotechnical observations was 
to monitor the geotechnical engineering aspects of the driven pile foundation installation 
for conformance with the plans and specifications and to provide supplemental 
recommendations, as appropriate. In addition, we provided “Special Inspection” 
services in general accordance with Section 1705.7 of the 2018 International Building 
Code by observing the driven pile foundation installation for general conformance with 
the project plans, specifications, and geotechnical engineering report. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co 
Page 4 
W.O. 8120-10 (Pile Installation Report) 
July 30, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
PROJECT CONSIDERATIONS 
The proposed “Design-Build” project involves the design and construction of the 
Undersea Operational Training Facility (UOTF) within JBPHH at Pearl City Peninsula on 
Oahu, Hawaii. The project location and general vicinity are shown on the Project 
Location Map, Plate 1. 
The new Undersea Operational Training Facility is supported on 16.5-inch 
octagonal precast, prestressed concrete piles, designed for an allowable compressive 
load capacity of 170 kips (85 tons) per pile for the new building structure and 100 tons 
(200 kips) per pile for the new combat training tank (CTT). The Structural Designer-of-
Record is Coffman Engineers, Inc. The general contractor for the project is Hensel 
Phelps Construction, Co., and the pile installation subcontractor is Healy Tibbitts 
Builders, Inc. 
INDICATOR PILE PROGRAM 
An indicator pile program was undertaken with the initial indicator pile driving on 
November 2 through 4, 2020 followed by static load testing of two selected indicator 
piles (Pile Nos. 48 and 188) on November 16 and 18, respectively, and re-striking of all 
the indicator piles installed on December 1, 2020.  
The indicator pile program generally consisted of driving fifteen indicator piles at 
various locations across the Undersea Operational Training Facility project site. The 
purpose of the indicator pile program was to establish the driveability of the piles given 
the subsurface conditions at the project site, the selected driving equipment, and 
methods of pile installation. In addition, the indicator pile program also provided 
information on the driving resistance and contours of the load-bearing strata across the 
project site, which was used to estimate the length of the production piles. 
Hammer and Driving System 
Healy Tibbitts Builders, Inc. used a Delmag D30-23 single acting diesel hammer 
to drive the 16.5-inch precast, prestressed concrete piles. The maximum rated energy 
of the hammer is 66,100 foot-pounds at the maximum pump setting. The indicator piles 
generally were driven with the Delmag D30-23 on pump setting No. 2 (rated energy of 
44,280 foot-pounds) during the initial driving and then increased to pump setting No. 4 
(rated energy of 66,100 foot-pounds) during harder and final driving.  
A pile cushion consisting of 6 inches of plywood cushion block with a cross-
sectional area of approximately 342 square inches was used for the pile driving 
operations. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co 
Page 5 
W.O. 8120-10 (Pile Installation Report) 
July 30, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Pile Details 
The indicator piles cast for the Undersea Operational Training Facility consisted 
of 16.5-inch octagonal piles with cast lengths of 90 feet. The effective prestress level of 
the 16.5-inch octagonal piles are approximately 897 pounds per square inch (psi). The 
piles were casted from concrete with a minimum 28-day unconfined compressive 
strength of 6,000 psi. Therefore, the maximum allowable compressive and tensile 
stresses in the 16.5-inch octagonal precast, prestressed concrete pile are calculated to 
be 4,200 and 1,120 psi, respectively. 
The maximum allowable compressive stress is defined as 85 percent of the 
28-day concrete unconfined compressive strength minus the effective prestress value, 
while the maximum allowable tensile stress is defined to be three times of the square 
root of the 28-day concrete unconfined compressive strength plus the effective 
prestress value. 
Indicator Pile Installation  
A total of fifteen indicator piles, consisting of Pile Nos. 2, 11, 26, 29, 48, 56, 94, 
107, 125, 149, 156, 183, 188 and 193, were driven to tip elevations ranging from -73.0 
to -85.2 feet Mean Sea Level (MSL) at the locations shown on the Pile Location Plan, 
Plates 2.1 and 2.2. Information and other details pertaining to the indicator piles driven 
for the project are summarized in the following table. Detailed information is provided in 
the Individual Pile Driving Records in the Appendix for ease of reference.

Static pile load tests were conducted on two of the indicator piles (Pile Nos. 48 
and 188) selected by our office based on the fifteen indicator piles driven. Two 
compressive pile load tests were conducted on November 16 and 18, 2020, and results 
of the compressive pile load tests are contained in the following two reports: 
"Compressive Pile Load Test (Pile No. 48), FY20 MILCON Project P-463, 
SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility, Pearl City Peninsula, 
JBPHH, Oahu, Hawaii” dated November 25, 2020; and  
"Compressive Pile Load Test (Pile No. 188), FY20 MILCON Project P-463, 
SOF Undersea Operational Training Facility, Pearl City Peninsula, 
JBPHH, Oahu, Hawaii” dated November 25, 2020. 
Based on our observations during the indicator pile program, the driving 
equipment (Delmag D30-23 single acting diesel hammer) and methods of installation 
were acceptable for installing the specified production piles in general accordance with 
the intent of the project design requirements and the technical specifications. 
Production Pile Lengths and Pile Driving Criteria 
Based on the results of the static load tests and our analyses of the indicator pile 
driving behavior, penetration resistance and restrike information, we recommended 
using a production pile cast length of 82 feet for the majority of the site and 85 feet for 
the CTT portion of the site.  
In the event that some of the piles do not achieve the recommended termination 
criteria when the pile is driven to its full penetration depth, the piles may need to be 
evaluated further using the restrike blow counts after a minimum of 7 days to determine 
if the pile is satisfactory. If some of the piles are deemed unsatisfactory, the allowable 
compressive pile load capacity may need to be reduced based on the pile penetration 
resistance. Therefore, additional piles may be necessary to augment the reduced pile 
capacity to support the structure at the discretion of the Structural DOR. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co 
Page 7 
W.O. 8120-10 (Pile Installation Report) 
July 30, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Based on our engineering analyses and the indicator pile program conducted for 
the project, the following two pile driving termination criteria were established for 
implementation during the pile driving operations: 
The driving resistance must reach an aggregate of 12 blows for the last 
foot of pile driving for a pile tip elevation at -76 feet MSL or deeper to be 
considered acceptable; or 
the driving resistance reaches an aggregate of 60 blows per foot for the 
last foot of driving after the pile tip reaches Elevation of -65 feet MSL or 
deeper to be considered acceptable. 
PRODUCTION PILE DRIVING 
The production piles for the project were driven with the same hammer, a 
Delmag D30-23 diesel hammer, used to drive the indicator piles. A total of 196 piles 
(including the fifteen indicator piles) consisting of 16½-inch octagonal, precast, 
pre-stressed concrete piles were driven for the project between November 2, 2020 and 
January 7, 2021. The approximate pile locations are shown on the Pile Location Plan, 
Plate 2. A summary of the pile installation is presented on the attached Pile Installation 
Summary (Plates 3.1 through 3.8). 
Out of the 196 total piles, twenty-eight piles, designated as Pile Nos. 108, 128, 
130, 137, 140, 142, 144, 148, 149, 154, 155, 160, 162, 163, 164, 165, 167, 168, 170, 
180, 181, 183, 184, 186, 190, 194, 195, and 196 did not meet the pile driving 
termination criteria for pile tip elevations ranging from about -74.0 to -84.8 feet MSL. Out 
of those 28 piles that did not meet the acceptance termination criteria, sixteen piles 
were selected to be restruck, designated as Pile Nos. 128, 137, 140, 142,149, 154, 155, 
163, 164, 170, 180, 183, 184, 186, 195, and 196.  
Based on the restrike data and our additional analysis, we believe that these 
sixteen piles met or exceeded the allowable compression load capacity with a factor of 
safety of 2.0. The remaining twelve piles (designated as Pile Nos. 108, 130, 144, 148, 
160, 162, 165, 167, 168, 181, 190, and 194), which were not restruck, were determined 
to have been driven to adequate depths and penetration resistances to support the 
structural loads imposed on the piles with a factor of safety of at least 2.0 based on 
consultation with the Structural DOR. 
The pile driving operations were conducted under the near-continuous 
observation of a field engineer (Associate Special Inspector) from our firm and under 
the supervision of the Geotechnical Designer-of-Record. During the pile driving 
operations, logs were maintained for each pile, which included information pertaining to 
pile number, size and length of the piles, date driven, predrilled depth, blow counts, and 
observations during the pile driving. Individual Pile Driving Records are provided in the 
Appendix. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co 
Page 8 
W.O. 8120-10 (Pile Installation Report) 
July 30, 2021 
GEOLABS, INC. 
Hawaii • California 
Based on the observations of our field engineer and our evaluation, it is our 
professional opinion that the piles for this project have been installed in general 
conformance with the intent of the project plans and specifications and within the limits 
of generally accepted construction practices. Based on our observations of the hammer 
performance, pile driving behavior, and the pile load test results, it is our professional 
opinion that the piles have been driven to sufficient depths and/or resistance to provide 
the allowable design load capacity and/or allowable load capacity to support the 
structural loads imposed on the foundation with a factor or safety of at least 2.0. 
LIMITATIONS 
It should be noted that it is not possible to continuously observe all activities 
occurring simultaneously on a construction site. Our observation of the pile installation 
operations and related consultation services were performed in accordance with 
generally accepted standards of geotechnical engineering practice; no warranty is 
expressed or implied. Provision of construction monitoring by an engineer is not 
insurance, nor does it guarantee construction of any type. The contractor shall retain 
primary responsibility for the quality of the work, for adhering to plans and 
specifications, and for repairing defects regardless of when they are found. 
Hensel Phelps Construction Co
